      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/10427.James_Baldwin">About James Baldwin</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/10427.James_Baldwin"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1343346341p3/10427.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/10427.James_Baldwin">James Baldwin
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
7,099
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10528049054730755523"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217-master-list-of-author-disambiguation-by-spaces' rel='nofollow noopener'>See this thread for more information.</a></i><br/><br/>James Arthur Baldwin was an American novelist, essayist, playwright, poet, and social critic.<br/><br/>James Baldwin offered a vital literary voice during the era of civil rights activism in the 1950s and '60s. He was the eldest of nine children; his stepfather was a minister. At age </span>
  <span id="freeText10528049054730755523" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217-master-list-of-author-disambiguation-by-spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information.</a></i><br /><br />James Arthur Baldwin was an American novelist, essayist, playwright, poet, and social critic.<br /><br />James Baldwin offered a vital literary voice during the era of civil rights activism in the 1950s and '60s. He was the eldest of nine children; his stepfather was a minister. At age 14, Baldwin became a preacher at the small Fireside Pentecostal Church in Harlem. In the early 1940s, he transferred his faith from religion to literature. Critics, however, note the impassioned cadences of Black churches are still evident in his writing. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17143.Go_Tell_It_on_the_Mountain" title="Go Tell It on the Mountain" rel="nofollow noopener">Go Tell It on the Mountain</a>, his first novel, is a partially autobiographical account of his youth. His essay collections <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/410810.Notes_of_a_Native_Son" title="Notes of a Native Son" rel="nofollow noopener">Notes of a Native Son</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38458.Nobody_Knows_My_Name" title="Nobody Knows My Name" rel="nofollow noopener">Nobody Knows My Name</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/464260.The_Fire_Next_Time" title="The Fire Next Time" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fire Next Time</a> were influential in informing a large white audience.<br /><br />From 1948, Baldwin made his home primarily in the south of France, but often returned to the USA to lecture or teach. In 1957, he began spending half of each year in New York City. His novels include <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38462.Giovanni_s_Room" title="Giovanni's Room" rel="nofollow noopener">Giovanni's Room</a>, about a white American expatriate who must come to terms with his homosexuality, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38474.Another_Country" title="Another Country" rel="nofollow noopener">Another Country</a>, about racial and gay sexual tensions among New York intellectuals. His inclusion of gay themes resulted in a lot of savage criticism from the Black community. Eldridge Cleaver, of the Black Panthers, stated the Baldwin's writing displayed an "agonizing, total hatred of blacks." Baldwin's play, Blues for Mister Charlie, was produced in 1964. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38469.Going_to_Meet_the_Man" title="Going to Meet the Man" rel="nofollow noopener">Going to Meet the Man</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38461.Tell_Me_How_Long_the_Train_s_Been_Gone" title="Tell Me How Long the Train's Been Gone" rel="nofollow noopener">Tell Me How Long the Train's Been Gone</a> provided powerful descriptions of American racism. As an openly gay man, he became increasingly outspoken in condemning discrimination against lesbian and gay people.<br /><br />On November 30, 1987 Baldwin died from stomach cancer in Saint-Paul-de-Vence, France. He was buried at the Ferncliff Cemetery in Hartsdale, near New York City.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10528049054730755523" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1129041-the-fire-next-time">Quotes from The Fire Next Time</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;I imagine one of the reasons people cling to their hates so stubbornly is because they sense, once hate is gone, they will be forced to deal with pain.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/1867-i-imagine-one-of-the-reasons-people-cling-to-their">2410 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Life is tragic simply because the earth turns and the sun inexorably rises and sets, and one day, for each of us, the sun will go down for the last, last time. Perhaps the whole root of our trouble, the human trouble, is that we will sacrifice all the beauty of our lives, will imprison ourselves in totems, taboos, crosses, blood sacrifices, steeples, mosques, races, armies, flags, nations, in order to deny the fact of death, the only fact we have. It seems to me that one ought to rejoice in the fact of death--ought to decide, indeed, to earn one's death by confronting with passion the conundrum of life. One is responsible for life: It is the small beacon in that terrifying darkness from which we come and to which we shall return.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/2091-life-is-tragic-simply-because-the-earth-turns-and-the">817 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
